  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_c4ba9d70-59bd-4b56-8f72-2c230479dabd'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);

      initializeSiwa();

<span id="freeTextContainer16621627404279872936">Charlie Higson's <i>The Enemy</i> is the first in a jaw-dropping zombie horror series for teens. Everyone over the age of fourteen has succumbed to a deadly zombie virus and now the kids must keep themselves alive.<br/><br/><b>When the sickness came, every parent, police officer, politician - every adult fell ill.   <span id="freeText16621627404279872936" style="display:none">Charlie Higson's <i>The Enemy</i> is the first in a jaw-dropping zombie horror series for teens. Everyone over the age of fourteen has succumbed to a deadly zombie virus and now the kids must keep themselves alive.<br /><br /><b>When the sickness came, every parent, police officer, politician - every adult fell ill. The lucky ones died. The others are crazed, confused and hungry. </b><br /><br /><b>Only children under fourteen remain, and they're fighting to survive.</b><br /><br /><b></b>Now there are rumours of a safe place to hide. And so a gang of children begin their quest across London, where all through the city - down alleyways, in deserted houses, underground - the grown-ups lie in wait.<br /><br />But can they make it there - alive?<br /><br />This edition contains the first chapter of the second book <i>The Dead</i>.</span>

<a href="/questions/378115-i-wonder-why-achilleus-kissed-just-john">I wonder why Achilleus kissed Just John after they finished fighting. Does anyone else wonder that? Cause its pulling at me.</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_378115'><a id="like_count_community_question_378115" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/378115?resource_type=CommunityQuestion"><span class="likesCount">3 likes</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F8540357-the-enemy">like</a></span>

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/15619834-michael-silverman"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1442874322i/15619834._UX100_CR0,1,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/15619834-michael-silverman">Michael Silverman</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">It was a power move to show his complete dominance over John by humiliating him in front of his clan, as well as to establish his position within thos<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">It was a power move to show his complete dominance over John by humiliating him in front of his clan, as well as to establish his position within those living in the palace. It was a direct response to John who was certainly homophobic (based on a "projection" that homoerotic statements would rile Achilleus) and a display of Achilleus' apparent comfort with his sexuality (whether straight or not).<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/418692338?book_show_action=true">Sep 20, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Laura" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Laura" href="/user/show/4844873-laura">Laura</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781423131755" href="/book/show/7358135-the-enemy">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4844873-laura?shelf=zombie">zombie</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer418692338" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7960110714054690316"><br/><b>”We can’t lose all we believe in. Our sense of right and wrong, said Maxie. Just to survive.<br/>Just to survive? There’s no <i>just</i> about it. Survival is everything.”</b><br/><br/>Have you ever noticed that big budget everyone-is-pretty-as-all-hell-even-covered-in-blood Hollywood horror movies hardly ever kill kids? The kids escape, live to tell the tale, and walk off into the sunset with their “happily-ever-after” tucked under their arms. Well….let me say here and now—the same can NOT be said for a Charlie Higson w</span>
  <span id="freeText7960110714054690316" style="display:none"><br /><b>”We can’t lose all we believe in. Our sense of right and wrong, said Maxie. Just to survive.<br />Just to survive? There’s no <i>just</i> about it. Survival is everything.”</b><br /><br />Have you ever noticed that big budget everyone-is-pretty-as-all-hell-even-covered-in-blood Hollywood horror movies hardly ever kill kids? The kids escape, live to tell the tale, and walk off into the sunset with their “happily-ever-after” tucked under their arms. Well….let me say here and now—the same can NOT be said for a Charlie Higson world. The man has no problems slaughtering his characters—his kids. I realize that might sound sick, but hey, I’m talking horror here. haha… So yeah, I love the man already and this is just book one! :D<br /><br />Come on. Let me introduce you to Charlie Higson’s world! The Enemy pulls readers into a world a year in to a “disaster” that made every grown up 16 years or older sick, crazed, and diseased. Adults overwhelmed with madness tear through the streets of London with a hunger for blood and flesh. Mothers and fathers turn on their own children. Teachers show students whole new kinds of bloody lessons. Neighbors killing neighbors. So in return, the children must take up arms and defend themselves. Kids killing parents, brothers, sisters, and friends. Brutal, bloody, disgusting battles of survival that will rip your soul to shreds! <br /><br />All over London, groups of armed to the teeth kids have holed up to fight, work, and hopefully survive together. Readers meet two groups of kids banded together in supermarkets faced with hard decisions, low food supplies, and constant attacks from the grown-ups. When news comes down and around about a better place, a safe place with more kids, protection, and food—the kids decide to risk it all and head to Buckingham Palace. Yes, I said Buckingham Palace! Haha…Bloody brilliant, right? As a history geek, Higson is my hero. He has infused history lessons into a zombie tale! Haha…*bows head in awe*<br /><br />The groups of children range from the very small to the older teenagers in charge with life and death decisions of sacrifice and loyalty. Attack, RUN, fire, or die! Fighting the grown-ups is a must to live another day, but when the fighting, power struggle, backstabbing, and manipulation grow within the bands of kids, each one must learn to stand up, pick a side, lead, follow, or question. The kids always assumed the dangers would come from the outside—drooling, sick, mad, grown-ups trying to get in. But what if the enemy is inside, in charge or right beside you? Can trust and loyalty survive the bloodbath and slaughter of this zombie like disaster? <br /><br />Haha…I told myself I would not ramble on, but hell I haven’t even touched on the characters yet. Some of these voices and kids stole my heart right away while others slowly grew on me through the battles and chaos. Several were gone in a blink of an eye while others made me root, cheer and hope to see them lead in the future. So many kids woven together with their own voices, humor, and style. I loved them all! Each one contributed leadership, heart, intelligence, compassion, strength, and ingenuity. All coming to together to form a society. The way the different threads and ingredients twisted together here on the page was amazing! Brilliant! I have to shout love out for a few of my favorites though:<br /><br />Arran—A leader we all hope for in real life. One who pulls everyone together by example, strength, and teamwork. <br /><br />Maxie—The heart of the story for me. Pumping compassion and loyalty into the madness.<br /><br />Oh, Whitney!—haha….Girl, you are kickass! :D I would hug ya, but I’m willing to bet you would kick my ass!<br /><br />Small Sam—Too cute for words, little man! He tiptoed right into my heart with his tenacity and courage! <br /><br />The Kid—I can’t wait to see what this “half clever, half stupid, and half crazy” boy has up his sleeve. :) A character I kind of put in the same league as my love and obsession with Dodger from Oliver Twist. A character to keep your eye on at all times!<br /><br />And now to my personal favorite (If I was forced to pick one anyway.) ACHILLEUS! He forged a fierce path through this story with humor, strength, and blood. *shakes head* The boy made a dent in my heart the size of Texas! Hell, they all did!<br /><br />This brutal, no holds barred punch was filled with gruesome and disgusting detail. No illusions. No mercy. No pulled punches. Honest, bloody slaughter-like style that hit me in all the right places! This is their life now. Some kids could let go of the old life, accept, change and survive in the new brutal way of things. Others could not. Sad, bitter, and heartbreaking one minute—hilarious and hopeful the next. This story clawed at my insides in more ways than one….<br /><br />I am reading book two as we speak, so I’m sure you will hear more of my gushing soon. :)<br /><br />Will the gang survive the royal zombie treatment at the Palace? Hope you dive in and find out!<br /><br />Read it. Charlie Higson’s world is unforgettable. <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7960110714054690316" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_680515060" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/680515060" />
    <a title="carol. " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3978225-carol"><img alt="carol. " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1307934801p2/3978225.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/680515060?book_show_action=true">Jul 29, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="carol. " class="user" itemprop="url" name="carol. " href="/user/show/3978225-carol">carol. </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780141325026" href="/book/show/6605625-the-enemy">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">hard core zombie fans, fans of William Golding</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=zombies">zombies</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=end-of-the-world-as-we-know-it">end-of-the-world-as-we-know-it</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=urban-fantasy-ya">urban-fantasy-ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=skimmed">skimmed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer680515060" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer950576547068885089"><br/> <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380431031i/864693._SX540_.jpg' width='300' height='200' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380431031i/864694._SY540_.jpg' width='80' height='100' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380431031i/864695._SX540_.jpg' width='300' height='200' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380431031i/864696._SY540_.jpg' width='80' height='60' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380431031i/864697.jpg' width='120"' height='200' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><br/><br/>One of my least favorite books from 9th grade English class was <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7624.Lord_of_the_Flies' title='Lord of the Flies by William Golding' rel='nofollow noopener'>Lord of the Flies</a>. I hated its theme, I hated its deliberate cruelty, I hated its vision of an island that was about the exact opposite of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/233818.Island_of_the_Blue_Dolphins__Island_of_the_Blue_Dolphins___1_' title='Island of the Blue Dolphins (Island of the Blue Dolphins, #1) by Scott O'Dell' rel='nofollow noopener'>Island of the Blue Dolphins</a>, a far more preferable tale. <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6605625.The_Enemy__The_Enemy___1_' title='The Enemy (The Enemy, #1) by Charlie Higson' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Enemy</a> is <u>Lord of the Flies</u> amped up, and while adding zombies would seem a natural fit for addressing survival in a world without adults, not even the undead can (re)animate this into a pleasurable tale. <br/><br/>Essentially, <u>The Enemy</u> combine</span>
  <span id="freeText950576547068885089" style="display:none"><br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380431031i/864693._SX540_.jpg" width="300" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380431031i/864694._SY540_.jpg" width="80" height="100" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380431031i/864695._SX540_.jpg" width="300" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380431031i/864696._SY540_.jpg" width="80" height="60" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380431031i/864697.jpg" width='120"' height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><br>One of my least favorite books from 9th grade English class was <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7624.Lord_of_the_Flies" title="Lord of the Flies by William Golding" rel="nofollow noopener">Lord of the Flies</a>. I hated its theme, I hated its deliberate cruelty, I hated its vision of an island that was about the exact opposite of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/233818.Island_of_the_Blue_Dolphins__Island_of_the_Blue_Dolphins___1_" title="Island of the Blue Dolphins (Island of the Blue Dolphins, #1) by Scott O'Dell" rel="nofollow noopener">Island of the Blue Dolphins</a>, a far more preferable tale. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6605625.The_Enemy__The_Enemy___1_" title="The Enemy (The Enemy, #1) by Charlie Higson" rel="nofollow noopener">The Enemy</a> is <u>Lord of the Flies</u> amped up, and while adding zombies would seem a natural fit for addressing survival in a world without adults, not even the undead can (re)animate this into a pleasurable tale. <br><br>Essentially, <u>The Enemy</u> combines zombies with the world of adolescents, scatters in a generous helping of random violence, all in a base layer of basic prose. Something has either killed the adults or turned them into zombies, leaving small groups of children under sixteen on their own. The setting is basic urban survival, and a band of youngsters is steadily growing more desperate when a pied piper comes to lead them to London. Specifically, to Buckingham Palace--I suppose if you are going to hole up in the apocalypse, why not go big? There's a parallel plot with a member of the group, Small Sam, seeking to rejoin his sister Ella after getting separated, and another limited storyline that deals with a boy who didn't want to leave their fortress. Overall, while the plot wasn't particularly surprising, it does moves quickly, despite kids arguing virtually every step of the way.<br><br>There were a couple of interesting offshoots, but unfortunately, they were likely there as teasers, as they weren't addressed before story end. For instance, <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ why did the zombies carry away Little Sam and not immediately eat him? What were the grey beasts near the zoo trying to do? Why were the zombies in the London mall playing dress-up? Why were the grown-ups able to live underground but "melted" up top? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Most of these questions come with the Small Sam storyline, where he is too focused on survival to question the larger issues. To some degree, I like a story that doesn't need to explain everything, and allows the reader to puzzle out solutions. Yet, without integration into the larger whole, the questions seemed to mostly fall into the deus ex machina category of unexplained actions/events that propel the plot forward or solve Sam's current problem. <br><br>Hisgen clearly has a developed world vision, and despite the unadorned prose, is able to create an atmosphere of depression and even despair. Clearly, while all are exhausted, a number of the children are also emotionally overwhelmed, burdened with the lives of those depending on them. Atmosphere excelled, but as mentioned earlier, it's the kind of skill that will fail to entertain me. Add in a willingness to sacrifice characters and a scattershot third-person subjective narrator and emotional engagement becomes a critical problem. Perhaps the Small Sam storyline is done to mitigate the emotional distancing, but for me, it wasn't enough. Both times through I noted dialogue is done well--the voices did seem like kids speaking, and if it later treads into well-worn philosophical territory of defining humanity and rebuilding society, it at least takes awhile to get there.<br><br>The zombies are largely there as action propellents, inciting the kids into ill-planned action. Once they serve their purpose, they are largely left behind to focus on the social dynamics of the children, so zombie-fans beware. Were you questioning why I mentioned <u>Lord of the Flies?</u><br><br>Ultimately, it felt like a read for a more masochistic kind of mood--one where I don't mind the violence, the negative philosophy, the lack of emotional connection, the basic prose and too many teasers. <br><br><br>Cross posted at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://clsiewert.wordpress.com/2013/07/29/the-enemy-by-charlie-higson-or-the-masochistic-reader/">http://clsiewert.wordpress.com/2013/0...</a><br></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="950576547068885089" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <a title="Aaron Vincent" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2924544-aaron-vincent"><img alt="Aaron Vincent" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1360133074p2/2924544.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/115435635?book_show_action=true">Aug 05, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aaron Vincent" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aaron Vincent" href="/user/show/2924544-aaron-vincent">Aaron Vincent</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781423131755" href="/book/show/7358135-the-enemy">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2924544-aaron-vincent?shelf=dystocalypse">dystocalypse</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer115435635" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4436431498819022090">Perhaps the most brutal and goriest YA dystopia novel I ever read. It's bloodfest almost every chapter. The novel is jam-packed with things that makes peace-loving bitches wince. Zombie attacks, strong language[There is a line from a character that shocked the hell out of me: "I didn't like him. He's getting on my tits!". Fuck Yeah Awesomeness!] cannibalism, and gladiator, everything. It's bloody, dark, violent and best of all, it's pure fun. Definitely not for the faint heart and sensitive stom</span>
  <span id="freeText4436431498819022090" style="display:none">Perhaps the most brutal and goriest YA dystopia novel I ever read. It's bloodfest almost every chapter. The novel is jam-packed with things that makes peace-loving bitches wince. Zombie attacks, strong language[There is a line from a character that shocked the hell out of me: "I didn't like him. He's getting on my tits!". Fuck Yeah Awesomeness!] cannibalism, and gladiator, everything. It's bloody, dark, violent and best of all, it's pure fun. Definitely not for the faint heart and sensitive stomach[especially the self-righteous douchebags:]. <br /><br />Charlie Higson is a damn brave author. He's nonchalant about killing his characters left and right. He doesn't care if its a major or a minor one. He's a psychopath. He will let you get attached to the character first, then he will kill it. He's like "You're liking this character, eh? What you would feel if I do this", then he'll kill that character in a brutal way. Pure wickedness. No one is safe.<br /><br />I highly recommend this to those who loves Michael Grant's GONE novels. Both book shares the same elements such as big casts, in-your-face non-stop actions, kids going against each other, alternating perspectives, fast pacings etc. It's fun literature at its best.<br /><br />It will leave you exhausted but it will also leave you zombie-hungry for more. I'm effin ready for more bloodfest and in-your-face violence. The Dead, bring it on!<br /><br /><b>I dare you to read it!</b></span>

<div id="review_759923598" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/759923598" />
    <a title="Rick Riordan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25375513-rick-riordan"><img alt="Rick Riordan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442449448p2/25375513.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/759923598?book_show_action=true">Nov 08, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rick Riordan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rick Riordan" href="/user/show/25375513-rick-riordan">Rick Riordan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780141325026" href="/book/show/6605625-the-enemy">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer759923598" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1288186256154275979">The Enemy, by Charlie Higson. I got to hear Charlie speak at the Disney-Hyperion dinner at BEA in New York. He said he tried to make this book as scary as possible, and would read scenes to his son, ratcheting them up until his son had trouble sleeping at night. I figured this must be worth checking out! The best description I can think of: The Enemy is The Lord of the Flies with zombies. It’s set in London after a mysterious sickness has killed off most everyone over the age of sixteen, but lef</span>
  <span id="freeText1288186256154275979" style="display:none">The Enemy, by Charlie Higson. I got to hear Charlie speak at the Disney-Hyperion dinner at BEA in New York. He said he tried to make this book as scary as possible, and would read scenes to his son, ratcheting them up until his son had trouble sleeping at night. I figured this must be worth checking out! The best description I can think of: The Enemy is The Lord of the Flies with zombies. It’s set in London after a mysterious sickness has killed off most everyone over the age of sixteen, but left some adults alive as mutated, brainless creatures who want to kill and eat the surviving children. Gruesome enough for you? Bands of children roam the streets looking for food and trying to survive. One such group has created a fortress at a supermarket, but they are out of supplies and the situation looks grim, until a mysterious messenger arrives with an invitation: Come to Buckingham Palace, and you’ll be safe. Is it a dream come true, or a trap? The novel offers tons of nail-biting action. Be aware: children die in this book, sometimes in nasty ways. The violence is not graphically portrayed, but Higson presents a dark, scary future. Different families have different comfort levels about this sort of thing, which is why I mention it, but is The Enemy a page-turner? Absolutely!</span>
  <a data-text-id="1288186256154275979" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_308667807" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/308667807" />
    <a title="Jo" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2467655-jo"><img alt="Jo" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596119990p2/2467655.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/308667807?book_show_action=true">Apr 08, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jo" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jo" href="/user/show/2467655-jo">Jo</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780141325026" href="/book/show/6605625-the-enemy">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer308667807" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17904957664330642690">Can you enjoy a book where pretty much every one of your favourite characters gets chomped on by a zombie?<br/><br/>I’m going to say yes because this book was brilliant.<br/><br/>This book was genuinely creepy and I like to think I’m made of strong stuff. Unless clowns are involved… and boats….and, like, those huge Australian bugs that <a href='http://veganyanerds.blogspot.co.uk/' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>Mandee</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/5590906-reynje' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>Reynje</a> take so much pleasure in sending me pictures of when I’m expecting wallabies and koala bears.<br/>OK, actually…. Maybe I <em>am</em> a bit of a wuss.<br/>But one thing that struck me </span>
  <span id="freeText17904957664330642690" style="display:none">Can you enjoy a book where pretty much every one of your favourite characters gets chomped on by a zombie?<br /><br />I’m going to say yes because this book was brilliant.<br /><br />This book was genuinely creepy and I like to think I’m made of strong stuff. Unless clowns are involved… and boats….and, like, those huge Australian bugs that <a href="http://veganyanerds.blogspot.co.uk/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Mandee</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/5590906-reynje" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Reynje</a> take so much pleasure in sending me pictures of when I’m expecting wallabies and koala bears.<br />OK, actually…. Maybe I <em>am</em> a bit of a wuss.<br />But one thing that struck me about this book was how atmospheric it was. I know I made a similar observation in my review for<a href="http://weartheoldcoat.com/2012/01/30/this-is-not-a-test-courtney-summers/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener"> This is Not a Test</a>, but one of the first scenes (the bit in the swimming pool, for those who have read it!) was like the beginning of a horror film.<br />A group of kids are inside somewhere and it’s quiet. Too quiet. But they’re safe in here. Aren’t they? You get an idea of the individual characters. You have the leader, the cocky one, the cheeky two and the one who keeps looking over his shoulder. Better safe than sorry, right? And they’re all talking and sniping at each other and behaving like boys do. And none of them have noticed that something is wrong. Really wrong.<br />And that’s where I’ll stop.<br />I can’t describe it because I’m not a writer like Mr Higson. I mean, you’ve read my other reviews, right?<br /><blockquote><br />“He’d always been scared of the dark. His mum had told him not to worry.<br />‘If you can’t see the monsters, they can’t see you.’<br />Back then there had been no monsters. Not real ones. Only imaginary.<br />Now…”</blockquote><br />See?<br />*shudders*<br />[FYI: That quote is from my favourite scenes in the book. SO GOOD.]<br /><br />And also, it’s bloody disgusting. It’s <em>really</em> gruesome. We’re talking Yancey’s <em>The Monstrumologist</em> gruesome.<br /><blockquote>“The skin blackened, shrivelled and split, the overripe flesh inside squeezing out. His insides had turned to mush… Arran prodded the body with his trainer. As he did so the skin popped, a stream of pus oozed out followed by a bright pink blossom of soft fat.”</blockquote><br />I mean, that’s disgusting, right? That’s so vile. That’s absolutely horrendous.<br /><br />It’s also AWESOME. And that’s not even the best bit. That comes later and eeerrrrrrgrgrghhhh it’s brilliant.<br /><br />Mr Higson certainly knows how to write a story. The twists and turns were perfectly executed and, even though if you’ve ever read a zombook or a zombie film you may guess <em>some</em> of the twists and turns, it didn’t bother me at all. There were certain scenes and certain things that happened that had me completely thrown. Mr Higson really took the phrase ‘Kill your darlings’ to a whole new level. Or at least ‘Kill Jo’s darlings’… so, yeah, THANKS FOR THE ANGST, CHARLIE HIGSON.<br /><br />I think without Mr Higson’s attention to detail with the characters this could have fallen into the ‘Oh... a zombie book? Now that’s original!’ trap. I have lots and lots of notes about my favourite characters in this book but seeing as I’ve told you that most of ‘em turn into Zombie Snacks (similar to Scooby Snacks, by the way, but more…um, living) I’m not going to share my specific thoughts and feelings. I kind of loved every single one of them. Their back stories, their dialogue, their reactions to what was happening around them, how strong they were when…<em>things</em>….happened. Love love love.<br />But even though I loved a lot of the characters individually, I adored how they worked as a group. They all had their roles to play without it being cliché and box-ticky. Yeah we have the smart one and yeah we have the one who wants to go zombie hunting, and the one who isn’t sure what to do but everyone’s looking at for help? Yep, they’re there too. But it felt fresh and exciting and by the time I got to the end, I really felt like I was part of their group.<br /><br />Though, that’s probably wishful thinking because I would <em>want</em> to be part of their group. Because, if/when a zombie apocalypse happens, I’m going to be used for bait. I know this and I’ve accepted this. But maybe if I stuck with the kids in this book I’d last a <em>little</em> bit longer before they dress me in a bright colour and shove me out into the street before locking the door behind me.<br /><br />Anyway…<br /><br />You know that feeling when you read the first book of a series (although, from my understanding, they don’t follow on? Just the same universe, though I may just be telling you vicious lies) and you get all excited and giddy <s>and you look at every grown up thinking they might eat you</s>? I have it with this book and I’m really excited to read more because if that ending is anything to go on, a lot more scary brilliance this way comes.<br /><br />Oh and also; zombie monkeys.<br />What was that? You want me to elaborate?<br />No way.<br />If the phrase ‘zombie monkeys’ doesn’t make you immediately add this to your reading list, I don’t think anything will.<br /><br />Anyway, I’m gonna have to go because there’s this really creepy bloke just standing outside my house. I mean… what kind of grown man wears a St George’s flag t-shirt and oh my god, I don’t believe it! He’s just got his friends to come too and… nope, I’m not having this. Hold that thought… I’ll be right back.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17904957664330642690" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

There are only the kids left unharmed and now they have to survive daily life. With the threat of the grown-ups around every corner we follow a large group of children who are just trying to make it to the next day.<br/><br/>Dislikes:<br/>I'm a very character driven reader, and this book quickly throws people at you. So I found it a bit difficult to connect to anyone.<br/><br/>Likes:<br/>The wo</span>
  <span id="freeText8377024847805247878" style="display:none">3.5/5 Stars<br /><br />Summary:<br />This book takes place in dystopian London and all adults have succumbed to this disease, making them zombie like. There are only the kids left unharmed and now they have to survive daily life. With the threat of the grown-ups around every corner we follow a large group of children who are just trying to make it to the next day.<br /><br />Dislikes:<br />I'm a very character driven reader, and this book quickly throws people at you. So I found it a bit difficult to connect to anyone.<br /><br />Likes:<br />The world building was great and I appreciated the plot. The idea of this disease only targeting adults was also very intriguing. I ended up really liking Small Sam and his character development since we spent the most one on one time with him.<br /><br />Overall:<br />Liked this book, not the best dystopian that I've ever read but I am curious to see what happens in the rest of the series, especially since there are 6 more books. </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer963870986" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4011087494320694636">June 2016<br/><br/>This is the fourth time I've read this and I love it more than the first time. Can't wait to finally finish this series!<br/>~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~<br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1438810709i/15758143._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><br/><br/><br/>This series is going under my favorite YA zombie books. Even though I wouldn't really call the 'grownups' zombies, but oh well. It's gory, has plenty of action, has great characters, and I love that it takes place somewhere else besides the U.S. I also love the fact that a lot of characters die. The author isn't afraid to kill of some characters. It's</span>
  <span id="freeText4011087494320694636" style="display:none">June 2016<br><br>This is the fourth time I've read this and I love it more than the first time. Can't wait to finally finish this series!<br>~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1438810709i/15758143._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><br><br>This series is going under my favorite YA zombie books. Even though I wouldn't really call the 'grownups' zombies, but oh well. It's gory, has plenty of action, has great characters, and I love that it takes place somewhere else besides the U.S. I also love the fact that a lot of characters die. The author isn't afraid to kill of some characters. It's like how GOT is...so my tip is to NOT to get attached to anyone. I made that mistake the first time I read this years ago. Got attached to one specific character and Bam! they die. :/<br><br><br>Can't wait to finish rereading them all and I can't wait to get my hands on a copy of the last book in November. </span>
  <a data-text-id="4011087494320694636" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer16097656319466646003">When a mysterious virus turns all of the adults into kid-devouring zombies, the children must do all that they can to survive. Can they while out-running the adult zombies and find a place they can call safe? Read on for yourself and find out.<br/><br/>This was a pretty good Ya zombie book that was a different take on the zombie mythos. Definitely check this out if you are a fan of horror and zombie books. This book is available at hastings and wherever books are sold.</span>

<div id="review_126466157" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/126466157" />
    <a title="Erin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3947264-erin"><img alt="Erin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1389401312p2/3947264.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/126466157?book_show_action=true">Oct 15, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Erin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Erin" href="/user/show/3947264-erin">Erin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781423131755" href="/book/show/7358135-the-enemy">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">people who can handle blood and guts, awesome people, action lovers</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3947264-erin?shelf=amazing-reading-experience">amazing-reading-experience</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3947264-erin?shelf=great-characters">great-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3947264-erin?shelf=little-romance">little-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3947264-erin?shelf=girl-power">girl-power</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3947264-erin?shelf=poc-secondary-characters">poc-secondary-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3947264-erin?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3947264-erin?shelf=action-packed">action-packed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3947264-erin?shelf=multiple-narrators">multiple-narrators</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3947264-erin?shelf=dark">dark</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer126466157" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15837064863149894221">Aw yeah. This is more like it.<br/><br/>I usually read books that are more romance-heavy, and reading this has really proven to me that I needed a break. This book was SO GOOD, you guys.<br/><br/>I'm not much into summarizing, so in short: for some unknown reason, all adults and older teens (at the time the illness struck) have either died or turned into a zombie-like creature. They will kill and eat any children they can. The Enemy is about a large cast of young characters trying to stay safe by any means necessar</span>
  <span id="freeText15837064863149894221" style="display:none">Aw yeah. This is more like it.<br /><br />I usually read books that are more romance-heavy, and reading this has really proven to me that I needed a break. This book was SO GOOD, you guys.<br /><br />I'm not much into summarizing, so in short: for some unknown reason, all adults and older teens (at the time the illness struck) have either died or turned into a zombie-like creature. They will kill and eat any children they can. The Enemy is about a large cast of young characters trying to stay safe by any means necessary. <br /><br /><b> Favorite Characters</b><br /><u>Arran</u> The head honcho of the kids. He is the quintessential "leader" character, with a heart of gold to match. He gets much love from me. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I was genuinely shocked when he died, especially because it was so early in the book. I thought he was going to be the main character, I loved him so! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><u>Ollie</u> Ollie was pretty much the best. He's shrewdly intelligent, always calculating and quiet in the background. His motto: don't play your cards till your adversary has played <i>all</i> of theirs. He also is pretty sick with a slingshot, which I thought was a cool weapon. Ollie, I will always trust your judgment.<br /><u>Maxie</u> Maxie* is Arran's second-in-command. She's a plain-looking girl with a no-nonsense attitude, but when things start getting ugly (as they are bound to get in such circumstances) she's strong enough to retain her humanity, even as those around her slip into savagery.<br /><u>Blue</u> Hello, recipient of my romantic love. Although he's probably thirteen, so, gross. He's the leader of a semi-rival group of surviving kids and can keep his head in almost any situation. <br /><u>The Kid</u> OH MY GOSH, THE KID. And that's all I'll say for now, for fear of spoilage. <br /><br /><br />*tee hee... Edited this a month later, because for some reason the original said "Marcie". Sorry Maxie.<br /><br /><b>Best Parts</b><br />The beginning started with a bang. I was grabbed almost from the first page (the omniscient narration took a while to get used to) and thrown into the action. I don't think I handle stress very well, because I was shrieking and squealing and generally making a scene throughout the whole book, but especially during this beginning scene, which is a great introduction into the tone of the book:<br /><br /><b>He had the familiar look of a vegetable, or a piece of fruit, left too long in the sun. The skin blackened, shriveled and split, the overripe flesh inside squeezing out.</b><br /><br />I literally yelled "OH NASTY!" at that part, it was so revolting. And yet I loved every second of it. :)<br /><br />My favorite scene, however, took place toward the end. Two hardcore guys have an intense fight to the death. Oh my word. I could barely read it, yet I was fascinated. There was so much tension and repulsion and <i>the stakes have never been higher</i>. Shout-out to Achilleus, the fighter I was rooting for. Sorry you didn't make my "favorite characters" list, buddy, but sometimes you scared me. <br /><br />Also, there is a section with cannibals, which is a basic requirement for any post-apocalyptic story. Can't say I blame them for choosing that route. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[At first I was disgusted with Nick and Rachel, but on second thought, if the virus thing is caught when you go out in the sun, it seems to me that the only food you <i>can</i> get is kids who wander down in the tunnels. So it's gross and cruel, but I see why they resorted to cannibalism. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br /><br /><b>Problemos</b><br />Like I mentioned earlier, the narrative technique kept me at a distance for quite some time. It was omniscient to the extreme, bouncing from perspective to perspective constantly. Like, every other paragraph type of constantly. So for a while I felt detached from the characters and couldn't imagine caring about their deaths (BOY WAS I WRONG), but I eventually grew to cherish every small peek into their minds. The characters were pieced together one brief dip into their heads at a time. It was a <i>very</i> interesting way to narrate the story, and one I don't think I've come across before.<br /><br /><br /><b>Conclusion</b><br />The Enemy was a fabulous page-turner. It terrified me, it made me laugh (sometimes nervously, sometimes out of real mirth), and it made me cheer (WHERE MY LADIEZ AT?). <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[OH MY GOSH I LOVED WHITNEY. The part where she took down Pod and was like "who you callin' babes?" was outstanding. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> There wasn't much emotional depth to it... but at the same time, there was. I dunno. What I do know is that if the action gets any scarier, there is a chance the next book will make me pee my pants. Gah.<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ARRAN LIVES! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>
  <a data-text-id="15837064863149894221" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer319608265" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14752890029101880683">So good! I ordered the complete series before even finishing this one! I'm on #2 now and completely hooked! I've been in a huge reading slump the past year - trying and failing to get captivated by a book. This is the first one I've been completely lost in in such a long time and finished it in only a few sittings (I'm a slow reader too lol). <br/><br/>I love how in just a few pages, and with many characters to boot, you really get to understand and root for every single one. Which is likely not the best </span>
  <span id="freeText14752890029101880683" style="display:none">So good! I ordered the complete series before even finishing this one! I'm on #2 now and completely hooked! I've been in a huge reading slump the past year - trying and failing to get captivated by a book. This is the first one I've been completely lost in in such a long time and finished it in only a few sittings (I'm a slow reader too lol). <br /><br />I love how in just a few pages, and with many characters to boot, you really get to understand and root for every single one. Which is likely not the best idea seeing as this author KILLS. A LOT! It stings! But... I love how brutal, realistic, and horrific it all is. You start to feel the loss that these kids are all feeling. It's gutsy and awesome! There's also a good dose of humor, witty banter, tons of personality, and strong friendships that are bonded from the need to survive and create some sort of stability (however small) into a world that has spun out of control. Definitely a must read for any post-apocalyptic fan!</span>
  <a data-text-id="14752890029101880683" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2186641561" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer3660001127012241211">I love zombie apocalypse in all media apart from in books, it seems. I find the high-action scenes that work so well on screen fail to appeal to me in quite the same way, in literary format. This is entirely a personal preference and found this book excellently executed in what it was (as all the other rave reviews will attest to) but was merely not the read for me.<br/><br/>This did, however, manage to provide the creep-factor I <i>do</i> love in my fiction, on multiple occasions, and created a startlingly blea</span>
  <span id="freeText3660001127012241211" style="display:none">I love zombie apocalypse in all media apart from in books, it seems. I find the high-action scenes that work so well on screen fail to appeal to me in quite the same way, in literary format. This is entirely a personal preference and found this book excellently executed in what it was (as all the other rave reviews will attest to) but was merely not the read for me.<br /><br />This did, however, manage to provide the creep-factor I <i>do</i> love in my fiction, on multiple occasions, and created a startlingly bleak yet vividly realistic future landscape, with a lovable band of rogues, in which to bring this dystopia to life.</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781423133124" href="/book/show/9532750-the-enemy">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16362475-emily?shelf=pageturner">pageturner</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16362475-emily?shelf=books-that-made-me-laugh">books-that-made-me-laugh</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer613672770" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer10810570395726229641">I enjoyed this book so much! Characters are killed left and right, and none of the horrible details are left out. It's gory, brutal, slightly gross at times - just how I like it. The writing, guys, is just fantastic! There's nothing "special" about it: there's no flowery prose or philosophical quotes to hang on my wall, instead it's fast-paced and drew me in so fast! Higson has this way of writing that makes it feel so <i> real</i>. One moment I'm with Maxie and her gang, and in the next paragraph I ca</span>
  <span id="freeText10810570395726229641" style="display:none">I enjoyed this book so much! Characters are killed left and right, and none of the horrible details are left out. It's gory, brutal, slightly gross at times - just how I like it. The writing, guys, is just fantastic! There's nothing "special" about it: there's no flowery prose or philosophical quotes to hang on my wall, instead it's fast-paced and drew me in so fast! Higson has this way of writing that makes it feel so <i> real</i>. One moment I'm with Maxie and her gang, and in the next paragraph I can be a kid seeing grown-ups approach. It just flows so nicely, action after action after bloody gory battlescenes. There's no filtering here. There's no "he got a wound and died", oh no no no. Everything is described, every single detail. At times I was so into the book I thought I would get anxiety attacks, because no kid was safe. One moment they were there and then they weren't. It's so <i>intense</i>! <br /><br />The characters had me rooting for them, and even though they could piss me off at times I just really love them all. As I said before, no kid in this story was safe, and every time someone died I would be getting teary-eyed and silently curse that fictional world for being so unfair. There were moments where I felt so happy for them, times when I wanted to hug them or help them kill some zombies, and all in all they were my friends. I miss them already! (especially you, Achilleus)</span>

<div id="review_910409176" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/910409176" />
    <a title="K." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5663034-k"><img alt="K." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1525318510p2/5663034.jpg" /></a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5663034-k?shelf=2014">2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5663034-k?shelf=own-it-hard-copy">own-it-hard-copy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5663034-k?shelf=2020">2020</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5663034-k?shelf=setting-uk">setting-uk</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5663034-k?shelf=2016">2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5663034-k?shelf=own-it-kindle">own-it-kindle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5663034-k?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5663034-k?shelf=audience-young-adult">audience-young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5663034-k?shelf=dystopian">dystopian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5663034-k?shelf=horror">horror</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer910409176" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8153571107614802200">Trigger warnings: gore, death, violence, death of a child, cannibalism, zombies, seriously y'all there is LOTS of death and violence and gore, death of a parent (in the past). <br/><br/>7/10/2020<br/>Public service announcement: Don't eat while you're reading this. <br/><br/>7/4/2016<br/>I stand by everything I said about this book last time around. Except that this time, I adopted a don't-read-before-bed strategy to avoid the nightmares, which was incredibly successful. HURRAH. <br/><br/>It's such a fast paced and engaging story, and</span>
  <span id="freeText8153571107614802200" style="display:none">Trigger warnings: gore, death, violence, death of a child, cannibalism, zombies, seriously y'all there is LOTS of death and violence and gore, death of a parent (in the past). <br /><br />7/10/2020<br />Public service announcement: Don't eat while you're reading this. <br /><br />7/4/2016<br />I stand by everything I said about this book last time around. Except that this time, I adopted a don't-read-before-bed strategy to avoid the nightmares, which was incredibly successful. HURRAH. <br /><br />It's such a fast paced and engaging story, and I was on the edge of my seat for the duration of the book. There are characters you'll hate but can still feel for, and characters you just want to hug, and characters you'll be terrified for. It's gory and violent and creepy and gross, but I just couldn't put it down. And I think I'm going to try and read one of these books a week over the next six weeks to keep the story fresh in my mind. <br /><br />27/4/2014<br />Holy crap. This is quite possibly the most terrifying book I've ever read, and it's YA. This book gave me nightmares about zombies. Of the wake-up-at-2am-sitting-bolt-upright-in-bed-with-your-heart-pounding variety. The kind where it takes you an hour and 60 pages of a happy adorable squee-worthy book to calm you down enough that you can actually get back to sleep. Admittedly, zombies are my personal squick, but this book is still terrifying. <br /><br />If you're squeamish, this book is not for you. This book is like The Walking Dead meets Lord of the Flies. The zombies ooze and drip various substances (and occasionally burst). Kids get eaten, attacked by dogs, attacked by each other, shot, bitten, held prisoner and are generally living in squalor. And when I say kids, I don't mean teenagers. One character in particular reveals towards the end of the book that he's only nine, which practically ripped my heart out of my chest because OMG NO NINE YEAR OLD SHOULD HAVE TO GO THROUGH ANY OF WHAT HE'S BEEN THROUGH IN THE COURSE OF THIS BOOK. <br /><br />It felt quite similar to Michael Grant's Gone series a lot of the time - a world where anyone older than 15 is gone and where kids are fighting for survival and to find food and water and a sense of stability - but with a better sense of organisation. The older kids look out for the younger ones and try to keep them safe as much as possible. Despite knowing that there's no one to stop them from smoking or drinking, no one seems to be doing so, perhaps because it would lead to increased vulnerability from the grown ups. <br /><br />I wasn't expecting to like this, given that zombies freak me the hell out. And I'm not even sure that I *did* enjoy it - it's a brutal and often terrifying book from start to finish. But it WAS well written, filled with incredible characters, and (I really hate this "word" but there's no other way of putting it) unputdownable. Despite my zombie squick, I'm going to keep reading the series because OMG I HAVE TO KNOW WHAT HAPPENS. <br /><br />Warning: do not become attached to anyone. They will probably die. Messily.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText13989950877241027520" style="display:none">This book has been sitting on my bookshelf since last Spring.<br />I feel like a complete idiot.<br />I absolutely LOVED this book.<br />Without a doubt my favorite book of 2011 so far.<br />Seriously my mind is blown.<br />This book was crazy.<br /><br />I have never read a book that has kept me up at because it freaked me out so much.<br />I usually don't get freaked out easily, but The Enemy was definitely freaky.<br />Not to mention gross, whatever you do, don't read this book while eating.<br />I made that mistake and couldn't finish my food.<br />But I have one problem with this book...<br />I cannot decide which character I loved more.<br />There are three characters that I absolutely loved.<br />I loved Maxie because her character is crazy tough <br />and yet it stills shows you that she has her girl moments,<br />But then she freaking means business when there is crap to be dealt with.<br />I loved Small Sam because,<br />1. I need the second one RIGHT NOW!"<br />And since then I have not been able to think about anything but The Enemy.<br />Just you know what, stop reading this review, and go to the nearest bookstore,<br />and buy The Enemy. <div id="review_1547581279" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1547581279" />
    <a title="✨    jamieson   ✨" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7706640-jamieson"><img alt="✨    jamieson   ✨" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1499961431p2/7706640.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1547581279?book_show_action=true">Feb 13, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="✨    jamieson   ✨" class="user" itemprop="url" name="✨    jamieson   ✨" href="/user/show/7706640-jamieson">✨    jamieson   ✨</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/25849511-the-enemy">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=reread">reread</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=2016-reads">2016-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=action">action</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=apocalyptic">apocalyptic</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1547581279" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5323434247149654954"><i>
  <blockquote>“If a wolf attacks his sheep, the shepard kills the wolf, but he eats the sheep when he's hungry.”</blockquote>
</i><br/><br/><b>The Enemy</b> is one of those books I really, really liked when 14/15. I read all the series that was out at the time, and then I had ..... <i>
  <b>THE READING SLUMP™</b>
</i>. So I lost track of the series and now four or so years on I was like, <i>hmmm, maybe I should check those books out again</i><br/><br/>Two things strike me about thse books: <br/><blockquote>1:<b>THEY ARE SCARY AS FUCK !!! JFC !!</b> <br/><br/>2: They're not /as good/ as I remember. But s</blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText5323434247149654954" style="display:none"><i>
  <blockquote>“If a wolf attacks his sheep, the shepard kills the wolf, but he eats the sheep when he's hungry.”</blockquote>
</i><br /><br /><b>The Enemy</b> is one of those books I really, really liked when 14/15. I read all the series that was out at the time, and then I had ..... <i>
  <b>THE READING SLUMP™</b>
</i>. So I lost track of the series and now four or so years on I was like, <i>hmmm, maybe I should check those books out again</i><br /><br />Two things strike me about thse books: <br /><blockquote>1:<b>THEY ARE SCARY AS FUCK !!! JFC !!</b> <br /><br />2: They're not /as good/ as I remember. But still pretty good. </blockquote><br /><br />Basically, it's about a group of kids living in a supermarket at the end of the world. All the adults have become diseased and ... started ... eating the kids !! and it's hectic. <br /><br /><b>THINGS I LIKE ABOUT THIS:</b><br /> → <i>fucking terrifying.</i> These books are so, so gory and awful. You got kids getting eatin all over the place, you got kids fighting eachother. You got cannibalism, you got psycho monkeys, you got disease and death and blergh just about everything other thing you can think of. I mean these books are brutal, you think your fave is safe because they're a ""main character"" but oooohh no. Charlie Higson definitely understands the concept of "kill your darlings" <br /><br />&amp;&amp; Aside from the fact it's gory, the actual ""zombies"" themselves are <b>INSANE</b> These are not just lumbering critters who you might run into, <i>ooh no. </i><br />These bad boys are INTELLIGENT. <br /> <b>THEY !! LITERALLY !! MAKE !! PLANS !! AND !! AMBUSH !! KIDS !! AND !! THEY !! ARE !! SO !! SCARY !!. </b> Not to mention some of it is told in the POV of a zombie, <i>shudders</i><br /> They make the Walking Dead zombies look like fluffy little bunnies. Like, these books are scary as all hell I am worried about Past Me<br /><br /> → Worldbuilding. Because, I know what you're thinking. <i>Another zombie book?</i> Another <i>kids alone without adults book!?</i> yeah, yeah I get you fam but listen these bring something new to the table. <br /><br />First of all, they're set in London. And along with the setting comes the general annoying propriety that is associated with Brits. You got kids from posh boarding schools, Kings and Queens, and it's full of British slang. It was a new twist to the tired, typical American setting and I liked it. (plus, the "hideouts" of the kids are something else, since this is London, hub of ridiculous and over the top architecture - the hideouts are <i> real neat</i> I mean, they're hiding out in Buckingham Palace its amazing. ( So on a side note, how come Rick &amp; Co from the walking dead haven't tried to shelter from zombies in the white house !?!) <br /><br />But aside from that, the development of the kids, the different groups and cultures that have sprung up in these groups is good worldbuilding. Each different group of kids has it's own customs, traditions, languages and while they're not /too different/ they all still have their quirks and its just interesting. The expansion of the world just in one book was great. <br /><br /> → ACTION. So much action, on every page. These are quick books because they're so fast paced and the pace never lets up. Something is going down on every single page and it's great. <br /><br /><b>THINGS I DIDN'T LIKE AS MUCH:</b><br /><br /> → Yeah, the characters. Just a bit of a letdown. They're not awful, not by any means. These characters pass, but they're nothing special. I don't feel any of them are particularly complex or well developed. They exist to propel the story but I just wanted MORE. I wanted more from them, I wanted more about how the apocalypse if effecting them, how they feel, what they stand for. Don't get me wrong because we do get it, I just wanted much MORE to really develop them. <br /><br />And on another note with characters, I wanted to mention diversity because I felt, for a book written in 2010 when diversity wasn't so much of a big deal it's pretty good. I would have liked to see more <b>anD I COMPLETELY FORGOT FROM THE FIRST TIME I READ IT THAT AKKIE KISSES JOHN AND I THINK IT WAS A /JOKE/ AND HE WAS JUST ESTABLISHING HIMSELF AND I DON'T REMEMBER IT BEING A THING LATER ON BUT I WISH IT WAS BECAUSE WHEN HE DID THAT I WAS LIKE ?!?! </b>#GiveAchilleusABoyfriend<br /><br /> → Representation of women. I just, eh eh eh. I don't wanna say too much about it but it was a bit disappointing that there are very very female characters in this and the ones that are there are often given the "mothering" role and while Maxie is the leader of the Waitrose kids by the end, no one really respects her and I just eh eh eh. It was okay, but it was kinda off too. <br /><br /><br />♦♦♦♦♦♦♦♦♦♦♦♦♦<br /><br />Anyway, overrall I'd give this a <b>3.5</b> I think these books are genuinely terrifying, and a great addition to a genre thats overcrowded, especially in recent years with the rise in popularity of The Walking Dead. Regardless, I'm glad I reread this and while it wasn't as great as I remembered, it was still pretty good. </span>
  <a data-text-id="5323434247149654954" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer5450408320645679557">The story of Dognut, Courtney and a few others in their search for Brooke. Their journey takes them across London encountering other groups of children and sickos. These groups are interesting because they have evolved into differing formats. Some political, some warrior like, some regal, some technical. Each group has its own way of running things and thinks that it has chosen the best methods to survive. The `leaders' of these groups have different agendas too with some just wanting to keep th</span>
  <span id="freeText5450408320645679557" style="display:none">The story of Dognut, Courtney and a few others in their search for Brooke. Their journey takes them across London encountering other groups of children and sickos. These groups are interesting because they have evolved into differing formats. Some political, some warrior like, some regal, some technical. Each group has its own way of running things and thinks that it has chosen the best methods to survive. The `leaders' of these groups have different agendas too with some just wanting to keep their pocket of survivors alive, some wanting action, and others wanting power over others. Several things become apparent in that no one particular method is the `correct' method, power may not be as glamorous as it seems, and some people don't care who they tread on to get what they want. This topic opens up quite well and is easy to understand from the way events unfold.<br />The blood, guts, puss and general gore is there for those that want it. One bit almost had me putting the book down until I had finished my left over curry that I was having for lunch at work. It was particularly sickening whilst trying to eat. The `zombies' sometimes behave slightly differently to your usual brainless eating machines too.<br /></span>

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781423133124" href="/book/show/9532750-the-enemy">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6857324-lauren-stoolfire?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6857324-lauren-stoolfire?shelf=post-apocalyptic">post-apocalyptic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6857324-lauren-stoolfire?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6857324-lauren-stoolfire?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6857324-lauren-stoolfire?shelf=zombies">zombies</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1094856394" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3130550227090422598"><i>The Enemy</i> by Charlie Higson is set during the middle of the zombie apocalypse in London, England and follows teen survivors. The zombie apocalypse came about due to a disease that only affected the adults who slowly deteriorated into mindless flesh-eating zombies. The main group of survivors have holed up in a supermarket, so when another group comes and offers them refuge at Buckingham Palace, they begin the dangerous trek across the city in hopes of finding sanctuary.<br/><br/>I plowed through this 448 </span>
  <span id="freeText3130550227090422598" style="display:none"><i>The Enemy</i> by Charlie Higson is set during the middle of the zombie apocalypse in London, England and follows teen survivors. The zombie apocalypse came about due to a disease that only affected the adults who slowly deteriorated into mindless flesh-eating zombies. The main group of survivors have holed up in a supermarket, so when another group comes and offers them refuge at Buckingham Palace, they begin the dangerous trek across the city in hopes of finding sanctuary.<br /><br />I plowed through this 448 page novel in two days - it's that fast-paced and addicting. I didn't want to stop turning the pages. While thrilling and a good take on zombies, the storyline felt a little too familiar and it was difficult for me to fully connect with anyone from the cast. However, the last hundred pages or so took everything up and even and made me bump my rating up to a full four stars. If you're a fan of <i>The Walking Dead</i>, you may like to begin this series opener. I believe I will be continuing on with it eventually.<br /><br />My review can also be found on my <a href="http://never-anyone-else.blogspot.com/2016/10/chicken-challenge-read-along-wrap-up.html" rel="nofollow noopener">blog</a>.<br /></span>

          </span>

Sometimes when I read books with younger characters it feels like it's been written for a younger audience but not so with this one. I really liked the writing and the characters. <div id="review_1117642692" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1117642692" />
    <a title="Lazybee" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19638596-lazybee"><img alt="Lazybee" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1534308634p2/19638596.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1117642692?book_show_action=true">Nov 28, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
